Prompt: 'What are the types of Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease?\n' 

Generated text: '\nA:\n\nQuick Answer\n\nIn Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease, amyloid deposits form in the brain and spinal cord, and it is characterized by symptoms such as dementia, muscle weakness, abnormal behaviour and abnormal mental status.\n\nKeep Learning\n\nCreutzfeldt-Jakob disease is an inherited neurodegenerative disease, which means it is caused by a mutation in a gene. People inherit two copies of the gene from each parent, and each one of these copies can contain one or two mutations.\n\nPeople with one mutated copy of the gene, which is inherited from their father, are at risk of developing Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease. The risk of developing this condition is greater if the mutated copy is inherited from the mother because a child inherits two copies of the gene from both parents.\n\nPeople with two mutated copies of the gene are considered to have two separate types of the disease. The two types are sporadic Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease, which is a sporadic form of the disease, and familial Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease, which is a family form of the disease.\n\nThe two types of Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease are considered to be quite different because the symptoms of the two types vary. For example, people with sporadic Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease usually develop signs of dementia and mental decline after the age of 50. This is not the case with people with the familial form of the disease, who develop signs of the disease early in life.'

Other common complications include a heart attack-related disability, congestive heart failure and heart attack-related death.\n\nKeep Learning\n\nHeart attacks can be serious, even if they do not cause death. A heart attack can be a life-threatening condition, and it is important to seek treatment as soon as possible. The Mayo Clinic advises that signs of a heart attack include pain or discomfort in the center of the chest that lasts more than a few minutes, discomfort in one or both arms, back or jaw, shortness of breath or coughing up blood. The Mayo Clinic also notes that people with chest pain may have other symptoms, such as nausea, lightheadedness, sweating, indigestion or back pain.\n\nThe most effective treatment for heart attacks is to open up the coronary artery and restore blood flow. Treatment options include angioplasty and stenting, and the American Heart Association notes that these procedures are highly effective for treating heart attacks. The Mayo Clinic notes that stents can be placed in the coronary artery to reinforce or widen the artery.\n\nOther treatment options include medications, such as beta blockers and calcium channel blockers. The Mayo Clinic notes that beta blockers may be recommended for people who have heart failure. Other options include the use of angiotensin converting enzyme inhibitors, which are also available in combination with a calcium channel blocker.'

Generated text: '\nHIV, or Human Immunodeficiency Virus, is a virus that attacks the immune system. It has an envelope around it that is so tough that it is impossible to break through. The virus attacks white blood cells, and can cause diseases such as AIDS (Acquired Immunodeficiency Syndrome) and lymphoma. Once it is in the bloodstream, it may spread to the nervous system, brain, liver and spleen.\n\nPeople who have AIDS have many illnesses due to the virus. AIDS is caused by the body\'s immune system becoming weak and unable to fight off a wide variety of infections.\n\nPeople can be infected with HIV if they have sex with someone who is infected with the virus. The most common symptoms of MS are:\n\nVision problems, including blurriness or loss of vision in one or both eyes, double vision or a feeling of being "tunnel-visioned".\n\nTingling, numbness or pain in the hands, legs or feet.\n\nBalance problems that make it difficult to walk, stand or balance.\n\nHow is multiple sclerosis diagnosed?\n\nA neurologist will review your symptoms and perform a physical exam. The inflammation can be caused by bacteria, viruses, or fungi. The most common causes are bacteria (Streptococcus pneumoniae, Staphylococcus aureus) and viruses (Human parainfluenza virus type 1, Respiratory syncytial virus). The common types of fungi (Candida species) may also be associated with laryngitis.\n\nTreatment\n\nTreatment options depend on the cause of the laryngitis and the type of bacteria, virus, or fungus involved. Treatment usually consists of rest and taking an antibiotic medication called an aminoglycoside. This is an antibiotic that is given by mouth. Taking the medication may help prevent a secondary infection of the larynx.\n\nRevision Information\n\nThis content is reviewed regularly and is updated when new and relevant evidence is made available.
